        }

          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;
          align-items: stretch;

        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

Yea, this looks like a missing retainResource call. The only place I am seeing we retain the graphics pipeline object is here.



<span class="line"><!---->Yea, this looks like a missing retainResource call. The only place I am seeing we retain the graphics pipeline object is here.<!----></span>



<br>





https://chromium.googlesource.com/angle/angle/+/refs/heads/main/src/libANGLE/renderer/vulkan/ContextVk.cpp#1848



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://chromium.googlesource.com/angle/angle/+/refs/heads/main/src/libANGLE/renderer/vulkan/ContextVk.cpp#1848"><!---->https://chromium.googlesource.com/angle/angle/+/refs/heads/main/src/libANGLE/renderer/vulkan/ContextVk.cpp#1848<!----></a>



<br>



<br>





angle::Result ContextVk::handleDirtyGraphicsPipelineDesc(DirtyBits::Iterator *dirtyBitsIterator,



<span class="line"><!---->angle::Result ContextVk::handleDirtyGraphicsPipelineDesc(DirtyBits::Iterator *dirtyBitsIterator,<!----></span>



<br>





                                                         DirtyBits dirtyBitMask)



<span class="line"><!---->                                                         DirtyBits dirtyBitMask)<!----></span>



<br>





{



<span class="line"><!---->{<!----></span>



<br>





...



<span class="line"><!---->...<!----></span>



<br>





    mRenderPassCommands->retainResource(mCurrentGraphicsPipeline);



<span class="line"><!---->    mRenderPassCommands-&gt;retainResource(mCurrentGraphicsPipeline);<!----></span>



<br>





...



<span class="line"><!---->...<!----></span>



<br>





}



<span class="line"><!---->}<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Now if you set up a program and issue a  draw call, you should reach handleDirtyGraphicsPipelineDesc() since pipeline should be dirty and we need to create a new pipeline. This new pipeline will be added to resource use list. Then if you issue  glFlush() and then make a very very expensive draw call that will take GPU a while to process . Because you are still using the same state, no pipeline dirty bit is set, and you will not retain mCurrentGraphicsPipeline with this current draw call. Now if you try to switch to a different program and delete the old program (or whatever takes that will trigger void GraphicsPipelineCache::release() call ), it should add the pipeline to garbage. Because the second draw call does not retain the pipeline, garbage code will wait for the first draw call to finish and destroy it. Now if you issue glFlush(), the second darw call is going to access the already deleted pipeline object.



<span class="line"><!---->Now if you set up a program and issue a  draw call, you should reach handleDirtyGraphicsPipelineDesc() since pipeline should be dirty and we need to create a new pipeline. This new pipeline will be added to resource use list. Then if you issue  glFlush() and then make a very very expensive draw call that will take GPU a while to process . Because you are still using the same state, no pipeline dirty bit is set, and you will not retain mCurrentGraphicsPipeline with this current draw call. Now if you try to switch to a different program and delete the old program (or whatever takes that will trigger void GraphicsPipelineCache::release() call ), it should add the pipeline to garbage. Because the second draw call does not retain the pipeline, garbage code will wait for the first draw call to finish and destroy it. Now if you issue glFlush(), the second darw call is going to access the already deleted pipeline object.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





That is merely a theory, so take with a grain of salt.  I think we need to either always retainResource(mCurrentGraphicsPipeline) for every submission, or when we switch out the current pipeline, we should add it to the  resource use list so that it will be tagged with the next submission.



<span class="line"><!---->That is merely a theory, so take with a grain of salt.  I think we need to either always retainResource(mCurrentGraphicsPipeline) for every submission, or when we switch out the current pipeline, we should add it to the  resource use list so that it will be tagged with the next submission.<!----></span>

I'm looking into this. After a failed attempt at reproducing this in a test, I'm having doubts of retain actually being a problem. When releasing the program pipelines, we add them to the context garbage, which means that they are deleted when the next submission finishes; the pipeline cannot be in use after that because it is already deleted. In fact, it looks like we never need to retain pipelines (nor need them to be Resources to begin with).



<span class="line"><!---->I'm looking into this. After a failed attempt at reproducing this in a test, I'm having doubts of retain actually being a problem. When releasing the program pipelines, we add them to the context garbage, which means that they are deleted when the next submission finishes; the pipeline cannot be in use after that because it is already deleted. In fact, it looks like we never need to retain pipelines (nor need them to be Resources to begin with).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I'm building (a recent-ish) chrome with ASAN enabled to see if this bug is still reproducible. If so, I'll see if I can resolve it with more retains (which I doubt). If that's not the problem, we'll have to look elsewhere.



<span class="line"><!---->I'm building (a recent-ish) chrome with ASAN enabled to see if this bug is still reproducible. If so, I'll see if I can resolve it with more retains (which I doubt). If that's not the problem, we'll have to look elsewhere.<!----></span>

I'm convinced now this is a SwiftShader bug. A fence is being signaled earlier than SwiftShader is done with the submission. Here's a cleaned up version of the logs I've placed to detect this:



<span class="line"><!---->I'm convinced now this is a SwiftShader bug. A fence is being signaled earlier than SwiftShader is done with the submission. Here's a cleaned up version of the logs I've placed to detect this:<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->=== SWS: event shared 0x6120001f5340 signal<!----></span>

<br>





ANGLE makes use of the pipeline in submission 27, then queues the pipeline for garbage collection. In (*), SwiftShader signals the fence. A little while later ANGLE notices that the fence is signaled, and duly cleans up the garbage. In (**) SwiftShader starts apparently working on submission 27, after it has already signaled it complete.



<span class="line"><!---->ANGLE makes use of the pipeline in submission 27, then queues the pipeline for garbage collection. In (*), SwiftShader signals the fence. A little while later ANGLE notices that the fence is signaled, and duly cleans up the garbage. In (**) SwiftShader starts apparently working on submission 27, after it has already signaled it complete.<!----></span>



<br>

In 



<span class="line"><!---->In <!----></span>





https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/angle/angle/+/3379231



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/angle/angle/+/3379231"><!---->https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/angle/angle/+/3379231<!----></a>





,



<span class="line"><!---->,<!----></span>





 an



<span class="line"><!----> an<!----></span>



<br>





optimization was implemented such that the excessive recorded texture



<span class="line"><!---->optimization was implemented such that the excessive recorded texture<!----></span>



<br>





uploads would get flushed early and submitted.  This caused a



<span class="line"><!---->uploads would get flushed early and submitted.  This caused a<!----></span>



<br>





use-after-free bug in the following situation:



<span class="line"><!---->use-after-free bug in the following situation:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





* Draw with pipeline A



<span class="line"><!---->* Draw with pipeline A<!----></span>



<br>





* Delete A <--- this puts A in the Context garbage list



<span class="line"><!---->* Delete A &lt;--- this puts A in the Context garbage list<!----></span>



<br>





* Upload a lot of data



<span class="line"><!---->* Upload a lot of data<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





At this point, the flush threshold could pass and the commands recorded



<span class="line"><!---->At this point, the flush threshold could pass and the commands recorded<!----></span>



<br>





outside of the render pass up to this point would be submitted.



<span class="line"><!---->outside of the render pass up to this point would be submitted.<!----></span>



<br>





Associated with this submission was the current garbage, including



<span class="line"><!---->Associated with this submission was the current garbage, including<!----></span>



<br>





pipeline A.  However, the render pass that uses pipeline A is still not



<span class="line"><!---->pipeline A.  However, the render pass that uses pipeline A is still not<!----></span>



<br>





submitted.



<span class="line"><!---->submitted.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Now if after some time the render pass is still open, but the "completed



<span class="line"><!---->Now if after some time the render pass is still open, but the "completed<!----></span>



<br>





commands" are checked (another set of uploads causing another



<span class="line"><!---->commands" are checked (another set of uploads causing another<!----></span>



<br>





submission, a query status check, etc), the garbage can be cleaned up.



<span class="line"><!---->submission, a query status check, etc), the garbage can be cleaned up.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





When the render pass closes next and is submitted, the implementation



<span class="line"><!---->When the render pass closes next and is submitted, the implementation<!----></span>



<br>





attempts to use the pipeline, which is already deleted.



<span class="line"><!---->attempts to use the pipeline, which is already deleted.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In this change, outside-render-pass-only submissions no longer reference



<span class="line"><!---->In this change, outside-render-pass-only submissions no longer reference<!----></span>



<br>





the current garbage.  This has the side effect that the temporary



<span class="line"><!---->the current garbage.  This has the side effect that the temporary<!----></span>

buffers used for uploading texture data won't be released early.  A



<span class="line"><!---->buffers used for uploading texture data won't be released early.  A<!----></span>

future optimization may want to separate the garbage list in ContextVk

to render pass and outside render pass garbage.

M105: Vulkan: Fix garbage collection vs outside-RP-only flush



<span class="line"><!---->M105: Vulkan: Fix garbage collection vs outside-RP-only flush<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In 



<span class="line"><!---->In <!----></span>





https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/angle/angle/+/3379231



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/angle/angle/+/3379231"><!---->https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/angle/angle/+/3379231<!----></a>





,



<span class="line"><!---->,<!----></span>





 an



<span class="line"><!----> an<!----></span>



<br>





optimization was implemented such that the excessive recorded texture



<span class="line"><!---->optimization was implemented such that the excessive recorded texture<!----></span>



<br>





uploads would get flushed early and submitted.  This caused a



<span class="line"><!---->uploads would get flushed early and submitted.  This caused a<!----></span>



<br>





use-after-free bug in the following situation:



<span class="line"><!---->use-after-free bug in the following situation:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





* Draw with pipeline A



<span class="line"><!---->* Draw with pipeline A<!----></span>



<br>





* Delete A <--- this puts A in the Context garbage list



<span class="line"><!---->* Delete A &lt;--- this puts A in the Context garbage list<!----></span>



<br>





* Upload a lot of data



<span class="line"><!---->* Upload a lot of data<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





At this point, the flush threshold could pass and the commands recorded



<span class="line"><!---->At this point, the flush threshold could pass and the commands recorded<!----></span>



<br>





outside of the render pass up to this point would be submitted.



<span class="line"><!---->outside of the render pass up to this point would be submitted.<!----></span>



<br>





Associated with this submission was the current garbage, including



<span class="line"><!---->Associated with this submission was the current garbage, including<!----></span>



<br>





pipeline A.  However, the render pass that uses pipeline A is still not



<span class="line"><!---->pipeline A.  However, the render pass that uses pipeline A is still not<!----></span>



<br>





submitted.



<span class="line"><!---->submitted.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Now if after some time the render pass is still open, but the "completed



<span class="line"><!---->Now if after some time the render pass is still open, but the "completed<!----></span>



<br>





commands" are checked (another set of uploads causing another



<span class="line"><!---->commands" are checked (another set of uploads causing another<!----></span>



<br>





submission, a query status check, etc), the garbage can be cleaned up.



<span class="line"><!---->submission, a query status check, etc), the garbage can be cleaned up.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





When the render pass closes next and is submitted, the implementation



<span class="line"><!---->When the render pass closes next and is submitted, the implementation<!----></span>



<br>





attempts to use the pipeline, which is already deleted.



<span class="line"><!---->attempts to use the pipeline, which is already deleted.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In this change, outside-render-pass-only submissions no longer reference



<span class="line"><!---->In this change, outside-render-pass-only submissions no longer reference<!----></span>



<br>





the current garbage.  This has the side effect that the temporary



<span class="line"><!---->the current garbage.  This has the side effect that the temporary<!----></span>



<br>





buffers used for uploading texture data won't be released early.  A



<span class="line"><!---->buffers used for uploading texture data won't be released early.  A<!----></span>



<br>





future optimization may want to separate the garbage list in ContextVk



<span class="line"><!---->future optimization may want to separate the garbage list in ContextVk<!----></span>



<br>





to render pass and outside render pass garbage.



<span class="line"><!---->to render pass and outside render pass garbage.<!----></span>

*** Boilerplate reminders! ***



<span class="line"><!---->*** Boilerplate reminders! ***<!----></span>



<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.

          border-spacing: 0;
          border-collapse: collapse;
          /* In the case when the autocomplete extends the
           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
